<Rating>4</Rating>< text>
Indian for the Non-Indian
As a "noob" of Indian cuisine I cannot speak to the authenticity of the food, I can only speak to what it tastes like on my palate.  I basically stick to the Chicken Masala or the Chicken Curry.  Both wonderful dishes on their own and in combination of the garlic naan that they have.  There are pros and cons to the chicken curry though.  The chicken is cooked thru a little better so the chicken is more tender and moist but if you are going into a client meeting in the afternoon, don't eat it for lunch.

Hot and Cool
Be aware, the spicy sauce, drum roll please......is freakin' spicy.  Go figure right? A spicy sauce that is finally spicy.  A little too spicy I may say, but it may be awesome for more manly men than me.  The good thing is, there's also a cool minty sauce to cool down your tongue if you accidently add too much spicy sauce!<//text>

< user_name>
Edward Lewis</user_name>
<Time>1416058231132<//Time><rating>1</rating>< Text>
I've lived here for almost a Decade. I've watched the quality of life, the quality of the park and the value of properties decline every year. The park is managed by Sierra Corporate Management.

Tustin Village Mobile Home Park is billed as a "Gated Community". The only thing gated about this community are the two black gates that swing open and closed 24 hours a day with anyone and everyone coming in and out. There is NO security. The Gate Code has been the same for 10+ years. I've watched people (who don't live here) bring entire families to use the pool(s) and clubhouse facilities. I see people driving through here who DON'T belong here. There's trouble lurking within this gated community.

I've watched many people forced out of their mobile homes by skyrocketing rent costs. New tenants are expected to pay $1,600.00 per month space rent in addition to any mortgage payment they may have for their mobile home. Rent goes up approximately $80.00 per month every year (May) like clockwork. Meanwhile, surrounding mobile home parks are under $1,000 for space rent and are much nicer with much higher property values.

I've watched more than a handful of people just walk away from their properties. I've watched the elderly, folks on fixed incomes, forced out of their homes. The rent keeps going up and the property values keep going down.

Why am I still here? I'm stuck. I'm upside down in my property which I shouldn't be. Because of the exorbitant rent costs, the value of the mobile homes here keep declining. The only way for me to get out at this point is via a short sale or move my mobile home to another park.

If you're thinking about buying at Tustin Village Mobile Home Park, please reconsider. You can find much nicer mobile home communities within a 10 mile radius that are not run by a firm like Sierra Corporate Management. Many are privately owned like the one directly across the street from us which is a night and day difference. Their space rents are under $1,000 per month with property values 2x to 5x more than what they are here.

In summary, Sierra Corporate Management doesn't care about its tenants. It's a profit making machine. It's a shame many of those profits don't find their way back into the park. This is NOT the place to raise a family, especially if you're on a tight budget. My suggestion is to look at the other mobile home parks in the area or go down the street and rent a 2 bedroom apartment for $1,600.00, you'll be much better off, trust me.<//Text>

< Review>
My name is Miguel, and I am an Internal Medicine Resident (PGY-1 categorical) at Fairview Hospital of Cleveland Clinic, Ohio.
As an IMG and applicant to a medical residency training program here in the United States, I was looking for clinical rotations last year. I was fortunate to have found California Heart and Vein Clinic to rotate.

During my rotation through Dr Chane‚Äôs clinic, I learned how to put the theoretical concepts into the practice of cardiology. And beyond the clinical aspects, I also learned how to lead an exceptional healthcare team and to optimize time during busy schedules.

Academically, we reviewed and discussed journal articles on current progresses in cardiology, as well as topics presented in congresses like the World Congress of Cardiology and the European Society of Cardiology. I had access to the current issues of the Journal of the American College of Cardiology (JACC) and other resources. Dr Chane helped me fine-tune my presentation abilities and grasp the most important concepts of the topics presented. I had the opportunity to write an article about one of the topics I presented; Dr Chane reviewed the article and we submitted it to a medical journal. Another very remarkable aspect of my academical training during this rotation, was learning to read echocardiograms and nuclear cardiac imaging in order to make a diagnoses.

What an excellent experience it was to shadow Dr. Chane! It was critical for my matching. The outstanding letter of recommendation he gave me added significant weight to my application.

I invite applicants to a medical residency training program in the United States to come a rotate at California Heart and Vein Clinic.< /Review>

< review>
Vons is actually a great supermarket. They have a deli, hot food case, sandwich deli area, prepackaged foods from the deli, fresh produce, organics, a florist, dry cleaner, lotto vendor, Jamba juice, panda express, Starbucks, sushi makers, pharmacy, bakery +++ this store is very clean and the staff can be friendly. There are some grouchy people but not enough to discourage me from visiting this store. You can actually get flowers cheaper at trader Joe's than you can here. From what I heard the pharmacy is kind of pricey. Also the parking lot is absolutely the worst feature. Be extra careful because it can be hazardous with people not paying attention. That said, I use to live around the corner and always walked to Vons. My biggest criticism is that they never replaced their bike rack. It was destroyed by a driver and ultimately removed. So if you're thinking about stopping in it is worth it. Try a low flow hour because they no longer have their self check out and peak times are crazy with long lines. My favorite items are the carousel ice cream cakes and the giant hello kitty balloons.<//review>

<user_id>101466442122096967700<//user_id><user_name>Percival Gonzaga</user_name><Date>1525742296771<//Date><Rate>4</Rate><review>What impressive about this particular Vons is that their fresh produce section is at the front of the store. Most and any other store would have them at the far side or even at the back of the store. So, when I come it, it just feels nice, healthy and open - it doesnt feel crowded at all.
I have been coming in to this store for about a 3 years now, and a lot has changed.
I love that they accept google and apple pay. You can also use those means to pay for your orders at their in-house Jamba Juice and Starbucks. PROTIP: you can pay for your groceries from these outlets, too.
The only one disappointing thing they did which i had wished they kept were the self check out counters; because most of the time, i just go in for 1 or 2 things, and i didnt have to wait in like to pay. These supposed express checkout lanes that replaced the self checkout counters are empty most of the time, and it appears that its just a place to keep returned items to be placed at the end of the day. So, what should just be a quick pick up, becomes several minutes waiting in line at a counter for someone to finish counting change to pay in exact amount.

Other than that, the manager is very friendly when i had inquired about a favorite drink they havent restocked - they restocked it!! - and it sells out fast. - they however havent been restocking or having the party tray mini rolls or the croissants anymore, which is my most frequent buy from there a couple years back, but still - their fresh items are great, and its conveniently surrounded by other shops where you can eat, drink or shop at while a friend or family member is restocking your home's supplies.< /review>< Pics>
